1.2 GLOBAL SECTOR REGISTRY
--------------------------

# Extends Vietnam 62 sectors into a global catalogue.

TABLE dim_sector (
  id                 INTEGER PK,
  sector_code        STRING,    # e.g. "banking", "ev_mobility"
  sector_group       STRING,    # "finance", "mobility", "healthcare", "public", "digital", etc.
  description_en     TEXT,
  capital_intensity  STRING,    # "low", "medium", "high"
  regulation_level   STRING,    # "low", "medium", "high"
  labour_intensity   STRING,    # "low", "medium", "high"
  digital_dependency STRING,    # "low", "medium", "high"
  safety_critical    BOOLEAN,
  public_exposure    STRING,    # "low", "medium", "high"
  notes              TEXT
)

# The Vietnam set is a subset of this (ev_mobility, logistics, etc.).
# For global coverage, add: oil_gas, mining, defense, etc.


1.3 ROLE FAMILY REGISTRY (GLOBAL)
---------------------------------

# All roles from VN HSE + global tech/business roles.

TABLE dim_role_family (
  id              INTEGER PK,
  family_code     STRING,   # "engineering_backend", "sales_b2b", "policy_maker"
  family_group    STRING,   # "tech", "ops", "leadership", "governance", "field", "support"
  description_en  TEXT,
  risk_profile    STRING,   # "low", "medium", "high"
  integrity_load  STRING,   # how much system integrity depends on this family
  automation_risk STRING,   # "low", "medium", "high"
  notes           TEXT
)


1.4 ROLE REGISTRY (GLOBAL)
--------------------------

TABLE dim_role (
  id                 INTEGER PK,
  role_code          STRING,   # e.g. "backend_engineer", "ceo", "truck_driver"
  role_name_en       STRING,
  role_name_local    STRING,
  role_family_id     INTEGER FK dim_role_family,
  seniority_band     STRING,   # "junior", "mid", "senior", "lead", "exec"
  remote_feasibility STRING,   # "onsite", "hybrid", "remote_possible", "remote_friendly"
  risk_behaviour_band STRING,  # "low", "medium", "high"
  criticality_band   STRING,   # "low", "medium", "high", "system_core"
  notes              TEXT
)

# All VN tech roles (Dev, Cloud, AI, Security, Ops, etc.) plug here.


1.5 SKILL REGISTRY
------------------

TABLE dim_skill (
  id             INTEGER PK,
  skill_code     STRING,     # "python", "negotiation", "fleet_planning"
  skill_group    STRING,     # "technical", "people", "management", "domain"
  description_en TEXT,
  measurement_method STRING, # "assessment", "kpi", "certification", "peer_review"
  typical_roles  TEXT        # CSV of dim_role.role_code
)


1.6 GLOBAL BEHAVIOUR & ARCHETYPE REGISTRY
-----------------------------------------

# Preserve Type A/B/C/D and 27 archetypes, but allow culture overlays.

TABLE dim_behaviour_archetype (
  id               INTEGER PK,
  archetype_code   STRING,   # "performer", "politician", etc.
  description_en   TEXT,
  base_risk_band   STRING,   # "low", "medium", "high"
  base_type        STRING,   # "A", "B", "C", "D" (dominant)
  system_effect    STRING,   # "stabilize", "accelerate", "fragment", "distort_signal"
  notes            TEXT
)

TABLE dim_behaviour_risk (
  id               INTEGER PK,
  risk_code        STRING,   # "intentional_delay", "fake_report"
  description_en   TEXT,
  category         STRING,   # "delay", "information", "politics", "quality", ...
  structural_root  STRING,   # "process", "incentive", "capacity", "culture"
  severity_band    STRING,   # "low", "medium", "high", "critical"
  notes            TEXT
)


1.7 CULTURE / VALUE SYSTEM REGISTRY (GLOBAL)
-------------------------------------------

# This is the abstraction layer instead of listing 7,000 cultures one-by-one.
# Each real culture maps to a COMPOSITION of these dimensions.

TABLE dim_value_system (
  id                    INTEGER PK,
  code                  STRING,  # e.g. "collectivist_high_power_distance"
  description_en        TEXT,
  individualism_level   STRING,  # "low", "medium", "high"
  power_distance_level  STRING,  # "low", "medium", "high"
  uncertainty_avoidance STRING,  # "low", "medium", "high"
  short_long_term       STRING,  # "short_term", "balanced", "long_term"
  communication_style   STRING,  # "direct", "indirect", "mixed"
  conflict_style        STRING,  # "avoidant", "confrontational", "managed"
  time_orientation      STRING,  # "monochronic", "polychronic"
  notes                 TEXT
)

TABLE dim_culture_profile (
  id               INTEGER PK,
  culture_code     STRING,   # "vn_urban_tech", "us_startup", "jp_corporate", "ke_informal_trading"
  display_name_en  STRING,
  country_id       INTEGER FK dim_country,
  value_system_id  INTEGER FK dim_value_system,
  urban_rural      STRING,   # "urban", "suburban", "rural", "mixed"
  generation_focus STRING,   # "gen_x", "gen_y", "gen_z", "mixed"
  economic_band    STRING,   # "low", "lower_middle", "upper_middle", "high"
  digital_profile  STRING,   # "offline", "hybrid", "online_heavy"
  notes            TEXT
)

# "7,000+ cultures" = 7,000+ rows in dim_culture_profile.
# The spec is exhaustive; the rows are data to be generated/fitted.


1.8 GLOBAL TIME / CYCLE REGISTRY
--------------------------------

TABLE dim_time_cycle_global (
  id               INTEGER PK,
  cycle_code       STRING,   # "day_morning", "weekend", "salary_week", "holiday_peak"
  cycle_type       STRING,   # "day", "week", "month", "season", "event"
  description_en   TEXT,
  macro_relevance  STRING,   # "low", "medium", "high"
  behavioural_load STRING,   # "low", "medium", "high"
  notes            TEXT
)

# Vietnam time cycles (Tet, flood season, etc.) map here with country_id = VN
# Others: Ramadan, Golden Week, Thanksgiving, etc.


=========================================================
2. CONTEXT-TO-BEHAVIOUR MAPPING (GLOBAL SHELL)
=========================================================

This is where country + culture + sector + role → behaves like what?


2.1 GLOBAL HUMAN CONTEXT
------------------------

STRUCT human_context_global:
  country_id        INT
  culture_profile_id INT
  sector_id         INT
  role_id           INT
  time_cycle_id     INT
  org_size_band     STRING   # "micro", "sme", "large", "mega"
  org_formality     STRING   # "informal", "semi_formal", "formal"
  job_security_band STRING   # "low", "medium", "high"
  enforcement_level STRING   # "weak", "medium", "strong" (rules enforcement)
  compensation_band STRING   # "low", "market", "premium"
  stress_band       STRING   # "low", "medium", "high"
  integrity_culture STRING   # "weak", "mixed", "strong"
  notes             TEXT


2.2 CONTEXT → BEHAVIOUR RULES
------------------------------

TABLE fact_behaviour_pattern_global (
  id                   INTEGER PK,
  country_id           INTEGER FK dim_country,
  culture_profile_id   INTEGER FK dim_culture_profile,
  sector_id            INTEGER FK dim_sector,
  role_family_id       INTEGER FK dim_role_family,
  role_id              INTEGER FK dim_role,
  time_cycle_id        INTEGER FK dim_time_cycle_global,

  # Output bands (probabilities / likelihoods)
  prob_type_A          NUMERIC,  # 0–1
  prob_type_B          NUMERIC,
  prob_type_C          NUMERIC,
  prob_type_D          NUMERIC,

  prob_archetype_ids   TEXT,     # JSON array of (archetype_id → weight)
  prob_human_risk_ids  TEXT,     # JSON array of (risk_id → probability)
  burnout_risk_band    STRING,   # "low", "medium", "high", "critical"
  churn_risk_band      STRING,
  political_risk_band  STRING,   # risk of internal group politics

  # System effects
  system_stability_effect STRING, # "stabilizing", "neutral", "destabilizing"
  execution_speed_effect  STRING, # "fast", "balanced", "slow"
  transparency_effect     STRING, # "increase", "neutral", "decrease"
  notes                TEXT
)

# Vietnam-specific HSE rules are a dense, high-resolution subset where country_id = VN.


2.3 PROCESS RISK: GLOBAL SHELL
------------------------------

TABLE fact_process_risk_global (
  id                 INTEGER PK,
  country_id         INTEGER FK dim_country,
  sector_id          INTEGER FK dim_sector,
  org_size_band      STRING,
  cycle_id           INTEGER FK dim_time_cycle_global,

  process_risk_code  STRING,     # reused from VN 196 codes + global additions
  category           STRING,     # "alignment", "approval", "ops", "tech", "market", "politics", "infra"
  severity_band      STRING,     # "low", "medium", "high", "critical"
  likelihood_band    STRING,     # "low", "medium", "high"
  system_level       STRING,     # "team", "department", "org", "sector", "national"
  notes              TEXT
)


2.4 POWER & INCENTIVE: GLOBAL
-----------------------------

TABLE dim_power_structure_global (
  id                 INTEGER PK,
  power_code         STRING,   # "formal_title", "informal_decider", "clan_power", ...
  description_en     TEXT,
  visibility         STRING,   # "visible", "semi_hidden", "hidden"
  stability          STRING,   # "short_term", "medium_term", "long_term"
  risk_band          STRING,   # "low", "medium", "high"
  notes              TEXT
)

TABLE fact_power_mapping_global (
  id                 INTEGER PK,
  country_id         INTEGER FK dim_country,
  sector_id          INTEGER FK dim_sector,
  org_size_band      STRING,
  power_code         STRING FK dim_power_structure_global,
  typical_entry_point STRING,  # "board", "regulator", "middle_management", "local_admin"
  typical_effect      STRING,  # "accelerate", "block", "distort", "redistribute_benefit"
  notes              TEXT
)


=========================================================
3. TRAINING DATASET GENERATION LAYER
=========================================================

This layer explains how to automatically synthesize training examples for AI.


3.1 SYNTHETIC CASE GENERATOR SPEC
---------------------------------

STRUCT training_case_global:
  id                    STRING,   # unique case ID
  country_iso2          STRING,
  sector_code           STRING,
  role_code             STRING,
  culture_code          STRING,
  time_cycle_code       STRING,

  # Human-level features
  behaviour_observed    TEXT,     # short narrative of what is seen
  pattern_flags         TEXT,     # JSON: { "DELAY_INTENT": true, ... }
  type_estimate         STRING,   # "A", "B", "C", or "D"
  archetype_estimate    TEXT,     # e.g. "politician+performer"
  human_risk_list       TEXT,     # list of risk codes

  # System-level features
  process_risks         TEXT,     # list of process_risk_code
  power_structures      TEXT,     # power codes present
  system_state_summary  TEXT,     # "info_bottleneck_at_middle_management", etc.
  time_horizon_months   INTEGER,  # 1, 3, 6, 12, 24, 36
  outcome_label         TEXT,     # "team_collapse", "stable_growth", etc.

  # Target outputs for supervised training
  target_explanation    TEXT,     # explanation in structured CEO language
  target_recommendation TEXT,     # recommended 3–5 actions
  target_risk_score     NUMERIC,  # 0–1 risk of collapse/major issue
  target_confidence     NUMERIC   # 0–1 confidence of label


3.2 GLOBAL DATASET GENERATION RECIPES
-------------------------------------

TABLE dataset_recipe_global (
  id                 INTEGER PK,
  name               STRING,  # "vn_ceo_training_set", "us_startup_pm_set"
  description_en     TEXT,
  target_country_ids TEXT,    # JSON array
  target_sector_ids  TEXT,    # JSON array
  target_roles       TEXT,    # JSON array of role_codes
  sample_size        INTEGER,
  balance_strategy   STRING,  # "balanced_by_risk", "reflect_real_distribution"
  label_strategy     STRING,  # "expert_curated", "rule_based", "mixed"
  notes              TEXT
)

# A generator process (outside this spec) reads dataset_recipe_global,
# samples from dim_* + fact_* tables, and emits training_case_global rows.


=========================================================
4. LANGUAGE TRANSLATION LAYER (EN ↔ LOCAL)
=========================================================

Goal: keep professional, neutral tone, avoid cultural bias.


4.1 TERM MAPPING REGISTRY
-------------------------

TABLE dim_term_mapping (
  id                 INTEGER PK,
  concept_code       STRING,    # "intentional_delay", "fake_report", ...
  terminology_domain STRING,    # "behaviour", "process_risk", "power", ...
  lang_code          STRING,    # "en", "vi", "jp", "fr", ...
  label              STRING,    # translated label
  description        TEXT       # clear explanation in that language
)

# Example entries (for EN and VI):

dim_term_mapping_examples:
  - { concept_code: "intentional_delay",
      terminology_domain: "behaviour",
      lang_code: "en",
      label: "Intentional delay",
      description: "Delays tasks on purpose to avoid responsibility or to gain leverage." }

  - { concept_code: "intentional_delay",
      terminology_domain: "behaviour",
      lang_code: "vi",
      label: "Trì hoãn có chủ đích",
      description: "Cố tình kéo dài thời gian xử lý công việc để né trách nhiệm hoặc tạo lợi thế." }


4.2 PARAGRAPH STYLE RULES (ENGLISH)
-----------------------------------

STRUCT prose_style_en:
  target_audience       STRING,  # "ceo", "ops_manager", "hr", "ai_engineer"
  tone                  STRING,  # "professional", "direct", "neutral"
  sentence_length       STRING,  # "short", "medium"
  avoid_terms           TEXT,    # words to avoid (e.g. "lazy", "toxic")
  preferred_phrases     TEXT,    # recommended phrasing
  structure_template    TEXT     # e.g. "Problem → Cause → Risk → Action"
)


4.3 PARAGRAPH STYLE RULES (VIETNAMESE)
--------------------------------------

STRUCT prose_style_vi:
  target_audience       STRING,
  tone                  STRING,  # "chuyên nghiệp", "rõ ràng", "trung tính"
  sentence_length       STRING,
  avoid_terms           TEXT,    # avoid moral language
  preferred_phrases     TEXT,    # e.g. "đề xuất", "rủi ro", "nguyên nhân gốc"
  structure_template    TEXT
)


4.4 TRANSLATION ENGINE SPEC
----------------------------

FUNCTION translate_concept(concept_code, from_lang, to_lang):
  1. lookup dim_term_mapping by concept_code + to_lang
  2. if missing, fallback to English + transliteration
  3. enforce tone rules from prose_style_* for target audience
  4. return label + description


FUNCTION generate_bilingual_report(analysis_result, lang_primary, lang_secondary):
  1. Build full report in primary language using HSE output format:
     - type + archetype
     - core problem
     - root cause (system vs person)
     - 30–90 day risk
     - recommended action
     - system impact
  2. For each section, translate concept labels using translate_concept
  3. Output two aligned sections: [PRIMARY] → [SECONDARY]

5. COMMERCIAL & PRODUCT LAYER (STRUCTURAL ONLY)

This section prepares the engine for productisation without specific pricing.


5.1 PRODUCT CONFIG REGISTRY
---------------------------

TABLE dim_product_config (
  id                   INTEGER PK,
  product_code         STRING,   # "global_ceo_console", "vn_hse_agent", ...
  description_en       TEXT,
  target_segment       STRING,   # "enterprise", "sme", "public_sector", "fund"
  deployment_model     STRING,   # "saas", "on_prem", "hybrid", "consulting+tooling"
  core_modules         TEXT,     # JSON array: ["vn_hse", "global_shell", "amos_core_bridge"]
  required_data_inputs TEXT,     # description of minimal data needed
  output_interfaces    TEXT,     # "api", "dashboard", "pdf_reports", "agent"
  notes                TEXT
)


5.2 VALUE DRIVER REGISTRY
-------------------------

TABLE dim_value_driver (
  id                INTEGER PK,
  driver_code       STRING,   # "reduced_churn", "faster_approval", ...
  description_en    TEXT,
  measurement_kpi   STRING,   # "churn_rate", "approval_lead_time", ...
  typical_improvement_band STRING,  # "5-10%", "10-20%", ...
  notes             TEXT
)

TABLE product_value_map (
  id                INTEGER PK,
  product_code      STRING FK dim_product_config,
  driver_code       STRING FK dim_value_driver,
  relevance_band    STRING,   # "low", "medium", "high"
  notes             TEXT
)

6. LINK TO AMOS_CORE AND ABSOLUTE-HUMAN

This block defines how this global translation engine plugs into AMOS_CORE
and the Absolute-Human engine without exposing Canon internals.


6.1 AMOS_CORE BRIDGE SPEC
-------------------------

STRUCT amos_bridge_payload:
  # What HSE sends into AMOS_CORE
  country_id           INT
  culture_profile_id   INT
  sector_id            INT
  role_id              INT
  system_state_summary TEXT   # normalized description of Ω, H, F, S, C*
  human_pattern_flags  TEXT   # JSON of 54 human risks + 27 archetypes + Type A/B/C/D
  process_risk_flags   TEXT   # JSON of 196+ process risks
  power_structure_view TEXT   # JSON of active power codes
  time_horizon_months  INT

STRUCT amos_bridge_output:
  # What AMOS_CORE returns (logical reasoning / scenario)
  scenario_explanation TEXT
  trajectory_options   TEXT   # possible paths with probabilities
  recommended_governance_moves TEXT
  risk_scores          TEXT   # JSON cross-domain


6.2 ABSOLUTE-HUMAN BRIDGE SPEC
------------------------------

STRUCT absolute_human_payload:
  ubi_scores           TEXT   # from Absolute-Human engine
  behavioural_pattern  TEXT   # from HSE behaviour layer
  environment_state    TEXT   # PSI-like summary if mapped
  current_cycle        STRING # C1–C7 equivalent for human

STRUCT absolute_human_output:
  personal_trajectory_explanation TEXT
  stability_risk_band             STRING
  recommended_interventions       TEXT   # biological, identity, environment
  notes                           TEXT


=========================================================
7. FINAL OUTPUT STANDARD (FOR ANY AI TRAINED ON THIS)
=========================================================

Every AI that uses this engine must format answers as:

STRUCT hse_global_response:
  audience_type        STRING,  # "ceo", "ops", "hr", "policy_maker"
  language_primary     STRING,  # "en", "vi", ...
  language_secondary   STRING,  # optional

  # 1. Human / role summary
  human_type           STRING,  # "A/B/C/D + archetype combo"
  core_behaviour_label STRING,
  role_context         STRING,  # "Role, sector, country"

  # 2. Problem & root cause
  problem_statement    STRING,  # one concise sentence
  root_cause_system    STRING,  # system-level explanation
  root_cause_person    STRING,  # person-level (pattern only, no moral judgement)

  # 3. Risk and trajectory
  risk_30_90_day       STRING,  # "low/medium/high/critical" + one-line reason
  key_time_window      STRING,  # "7 days", "30 days", "90 days"
  system_impact        STRING,  # team/org/sector impact

  # 4. Recommended actions
  actions_step_1       STRING,
  actions_step_2       STRING,
  actions_step_3       STRING,
  optional_actions     TEXT,

  # 5. Power & politics (neutral)
  active_power_structures STRING, # list of power codes with explanation
  political_risk_note      STRING, # neutral, pattern-based

  # 6. If no action
  if_not_addressed_summary STRING  # what happens if nothing is done

1. GLOBAL DEMOGRAPHIC ENGINE — FULL SPECIFICATION
--------------------------------------------------------------------

DEFINITION:
The demographic engine models population structure, behaviour, evolution,
and economic influence. It is a deterministic set of variables that explain
workforce, consumption, political stability, migration pressure, and
household decisions.

--------------------------------------------------
1.1 DIMENSIONS (PRIMARY)
--------------------------------------------------
age_group:
- child_0_14
- youth_15_24
- adult_young_25_39
- adult_mid_40_54
- senior_55_64
- elderly_65_80
- very_elderly_80plus

dependency_ratio:
- child_dependency_ratio (0–1)
- elderly_dependency_ratio (0–1)
- total_dependency_ratio (0–1)

fertility_rate:
- ultra_low (<1.3)
- low (1.3–1.9)
- replacement (2.0–2.2)
- high (>2.5)
- extreme_high (>4.0)

life_expectancy_band:
- low (<60)
- mid (60–70)
- high (70–80)
- advanced (80–90)
- extreme (90+)

urbanisation_tier:
- rural
- periurban
- tier3_city
- tier2_city
- tier1_city
- megacity

gender_ratio:
- balanced
- male_skewed
- female_skewed
- high_male_urban_influx
- high_female_service_work_influx

generational_behavior:
- boomers (slow-change, stability-seeking)
- genX (practical, conservative, risk-hedging)
- genY (mixed, adaptable, external-reference)
- genZ (fluid, unstable loyalty, digital-first)
- genAlpha (narrative-driven, attention-fragmented)

migration_rate_internal:
- low (<1%)
- moderate (1–5%)
- high (5–15%)
- extreme (>15%)

migration_rate_external:
- brain_drain_high
- outbound_low_skill
- inbound_migrant_population
- mixed_flow
- refugee_pressure

--------------------------------------------------
1.2 SECONDARY VARIABLES
--------------------------------------------------
demographic_pressure_index = f(dependency_ratio, fertility_rate, median_age, migration_rate_internal)

workforce_transition_tension = f(generational_behavior, technology_integration_rate)

household_stability_score:
- scaled 0–1 based on household_size, gender_ratio, fertility_rate, elder_dependency

political_pressure_index:
- youth_ratio
- unemployment_youth
- elderly_vote_weight
- urbanisation_shock

--------------------------------------------------
1.3 OUTPUTS
--------------------------------------------------
workforce_pressure (0–1)
housing_demand_pressure (0–1)
healthcare_burden (0–1)
social_instability_risk (0–1)
consumption_phase_class:
- growth
- flattening
- saturation
- contraction

7. GLOBAL INCENTIVE-STRUCTURE LAYER — FULL SPEC
====================================================================

DEFINITION:
Incentive structures vary by region, culture, political environment,
economic pressure, and social history. This module encodes how humans,
organizations, governments, and markets respond to motivators.

--------------------------------------------------
7.1 INCENTIVE FAMILIES (GLOBAL)
--------------------------------------------------
1. Western Incentives (US/UK/EU)
2. East Asian Incentives (Japan/Korea/China)
3. South Asian Incentives (India/Pakistan/Bangladesh)
4. Southeast Asian Incentives (ASEAN)
5. Middle Eastern Incentives (GCC/Levant/Iran)
6. African Incentives (North/East/West/South)
7. Latin American Incentives (Brazil/Mexico/Andes)
8. Post-Soviet Incentives (Russia/Central Asia)
9. Island-State Incentives (Caribbean/Pacific)
10. Hybrid/Mixed Incentives (globalized societies)

--------------------------------------------------
7.2 WESTERN INCENTIVE STRUCTURES
--------------------------------------------------
Primary drivers:
- merit-performance outcome
- financial gain and valuation
- career progression
- independence and autonomy
- personal brand reputation
- shareholder expectations
- regulatory compliance

Behavioural effects:
- fast decision cycles
- high accountability expectancy
- low tolerance for ambiguity
- competitive work cultures

--------------------------------------------------
7.3 EAST ASIAN INCENTIVE STRUCTURES
--------------------------------------------------
Primary drivers:
- hierarchy stability
- group harmony
- loyalty to organization
- respect for seniority
- long-term planning
- limited public conflict

Behavioural effects:
- slow consensus cycles
- high execution discipline
- low open conflict but high internal stress
- high risk of burnout hidden behind politeness

--------------------------------------------------
7.4 SOUTH ASIAN INCENTIVE STRUCTURES
--------------------------------------------------
Primary drivers:
- negotiation for advantage
- informal influence networks
- family/clan obligations
- adaptiveness under resource constraints

Behavioural effects:
- inconsistent process execution
- unpredictable compliance
- high improvisation capability
- high tolerance for conflict

--------------------------------------------------
7.5 SOUTHEAST ASIAN INCENTIVE STRUCTURES
--------------------------------------------------
Primary drivers:
- relational trust
- saving face
- low-conflict preference
- gradual change adoption
- desire for stability

Behavioural effects:
- slow confrontation
- risk of “silent resistance”
- politeness masking misalignment
- high group cohesion under supportive leadership

--------------------------------------------------
7.6 MIDDLE EASTERN INCENTIVE STRUCTURES
--------------------------------------------------
Primary drivers:
- honor and respect
- family power networks
- patronage relationships
- reputation in community
- zero-sum views in negotiation

Behavioural effects:
- fast shifts when power changes
- high volatility in alliances
- strong loyalty gradients
- high potential for narrative-driven conflict

--------------------------------------------------
7.7 AFRICAN INCENTIVE STRUCTURES
--------------------------------------------------
Primary drivers:
- community loyalty
- family/tribal network strength
- informal trust systems
- stability under uncertainty

Behavioural effects:
- decentralised influence
- inconsistent formal compliance
- high adaptability
- conflict surfaces quickly when incentives clash

--------------------------------------------------
7.8 LATIN AMERICAN INCENTIVE STRUCTURES
--------------------------------------------------
Primary drivers:
- personalistic leadership loyalty
- charisma-based influence
- negotiation culture
- tolerance for ambiguity
- community identity

Behavioural effects:
- emotional decision-making patterns
- volatile politics
- high narrative-driven behaviour
- informal systems competing with formal law

--------------------------------------------------
7.9 POST-SOVIET INCENTIVE STRUCTURES
--------------------------------------------------
Primary drivers:
- power stability
- fear of losing position
- elite control structures
- centralized decision-making
- survival logic under hierarchy

Behavioural effects:
- slow official cycles
- fast unofficial cycles
- high corruption pressure
- dual-system governance

--------------------------------------------------
7.10 OUTPUTS
--------------------------------------------------
regional_incentive_signature
decision_cycle_model
conflict_reaction_curve
coalition_stability_score
negotiation_style_profile
corruption_pressure_index

9. GLOBAL PSYCHOLOGICAL OVERLAYS — FULL SPEC
====================================================================

DEFINITION:
Regional psychology is shaped by history, trauma, cultural norms,
collective identity, instability cycles, and social expectations.

--------------------------------------------------
9.1 PRIMARY OVERLAYS
--------------------------------------------------
survival_pressure:
- wartime trauma
- famine memory
- hyperinflation history
- occupation/colonial history
- displacement history
Scale: 0–1

collective_identity_strength:
- strong (Japan/Korea)
- medium (Vietnam/Thailand)
- weak (US/UK)
- fragmented (Brazil/Nigeria/India)

authority_distance:
- low (Nordic)
- medium (US)
- high (Asia)
- extreme (Middle East/Africa)

social_shame_pressure:
- low (US/Europe)
- medium (China)
- high (Vietnam/Philippines)
- extreme (Japan/Korea)

risk_aversion_curve:
- stability-first (Asia)
- opportunity-first (US)
- relational-first (LATAM)
- survival-first (Africa)

--------------------------------------------------
9.2 BEHAVIORAL CONSEQUENCES
--------------------------------------------------
high survival pressure → fast emotional decision-making
high authority_distance → low feedback honesty
high shame_pressure → avoidance behaviours
fragmented identity → weak coordination
strong collective identity → high discipline + high burnout risk

--------------------------------------------------
9.3 OUTPUTS
--------------------------------------------------

====================================================================
27. FINAL CANON LOCK LAYER
====================================================================

Purpose:
Ensures all outputs remain internally consistent across all 27 layers and
cannot contradict any logic primitive already defined.

===============================
GLOBAL DIMENSION BASE LAYER v1.0
===============================
This block defines the 12 universal dimensions used by the global engine.
Every country, sector, culture, behaviour, and risk model attaches to these
dimensions. Nothing outside these 12 dimensions is recognized as part
of this universe. This maintains deterministic structure.

DIMENSIONS:
1. DEMOGRAPHIC_STATE
2. ECONOMIC_STRUCTURE
3. GOVERNANCE_STRUCTURE
4. POLITICAL_CYCLE
5. SOCIAL_BEHAVIOUR
6. CULTURAL_ARCHETYPE
7. INFRASTRUCTURE_STATE
8. TECHNOLOGY_STATE
9. MOBILITY_STATE
10. ENERGY_STATE
11. ENVIRONMENTAL_STATE
12. MARKET_BEHAVIOUR

Below is the full structural specification for each dimension.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. DEMOGRAPHIC_STATE
---------------------------------------------------------
VARIABLES:
- population_total
- population_growth_rate
- fertility_rate
- median_age
- age_distribution:
    - age_0_14
    - age_15_24
    - age_25_54
    - age_55_64
    - age_65_plus
- dependency_ratio:
    - youth_dependency
    - elderly_dependency
- urbanization_rate
- migration:
    - inbound_migration_rate
    - outbound_migration_rate
    - net_brain_drain
- household_size_avg
- labor_force_participation
- gender_balance_index
- workforce_type_distribution:
    - manual_labor_percent
    - service_percent
    - professional_percent
    - knowledge_worker_percent
- education_attainment:
    - primary
    - secondary
    - tertiary
    - vocational
    - postgraduate

NOTES:
Demographic_State feeds directly into:
- economic stability
- workforce capacity
- consumption patterns
- social tension probability
- political cycle stress

---------------------------------------------------------
2. ECONOMIC_STRUCTURE
---------------------------------------------------------
VARIABLES:
- gdp_total
- gdp_per_capita
- gdp_growth_rate
- inflation_regime:
    - stable
    - volatile
    - hyperinflation_risk
- interest_rate_regime:
    - low
    - moderate
    - high
- currency_stability:
    - stable
    - managed
    - fragile
- debt_to_gdp_ratio
- fx_reserves_months_cover
- tax_revenue_percent_gdp
- unemployment_rate
- informal_sector_share
- top_industries (list of 10):
    - industry_name
    - industry_gdp_share
    - export_dependency
- productivity_index (0–1)
- investment_climate_index (0–1)
- ease_of_doing_business_index (0–1)

==========================================
GLOBAL META-LAYER SYSTEM v1.0 — PART 2/60
==========================================

This block defines:
- cross-dimensional dependencies
- variable weighting rules
- deterministic interaction matrices
- causal propagation channels
- stability equations
- shock transmission mechanics
- drift vectors
- recovery pathways
- predictive coherence rules

Without these rules, the country engine cannot behave like a real universe.

---------------------------------------------------------
I. CROSS-DIMENSION INTERACTION MATRIX (12×12)
---------------------------------------------------------
Each pair of dimensions interacts in a deterministic way.
Below is the full matrix outline — later parts will detail equations.

Matrix cell meaning:
DIM_A → DIM_B = “changes in A modify B via rule R”

     DEMO ECON GOVR POLC SOCI CULT INFR TECH MOBI ENER ENVI MARK
DEMO  ---  A1   A2   A3   A4   A5   A6   A7   A8   A9   A10  A11
ECON  B1   ---  B2   B3   B4   B5   B6   B7   B8   B9   B10  B11
GOVR  C1   C2   ---  C3   C4   C5   C6   C7   C8   C9   C10  C11
POLC  D1   D2   D3   ---  D4   D5   D6   D7   D8   D9   D10  D11
SOCI  E1   E2   E3   E4   ---  E5   E6   E7   E8   E9   E10  E11
CULT  F1   F2   F3   F4   F5   ---  F6   F7   F8   F9   F10  F11
INFR  G1   G2   G3   G4   G5   G6   ---  G7   G8   G9   G10  G11
TECH  H1   H2   H3   H4   H5   H6   H7   ---  H8   H9   H10  H11
MOBI  I1   I2   I3   I4   I5   I6   I7   I8   ---  I9   I10  I11
ENER  J1   J2   J3   J4   J5   J6   J7   J8   J9   ---   J10  J11
ENVI  K1   K2   K3   K4   K5   K6   K7   K8   K9   K10  ---   K11
MARK L1   L2   L3   L4   L5   L6   L7   L8   L9   L10  L11   ---

EXAMPLE:
A1 = DEMOGRAPHIC_STATE → ECONOMIC_STRUCTURE
Meaning: changes in population size/age alter workforce → GDP structure.

Every lettered term (A1, A2, … L11) will be defined with equations.

---------------------------------------------------------
II. INTERACTION RULE TYPES
---------------------------------------------------------
For each interaction DIM_A → DIM_B, only one of these rule types applies:

1. Linear influence
   DIM_B += α * Δ(DIM_A)

2. Nonlinear threshold influence
   if DIM_A > T: DIM_B changes sharply

3. Directional influence
   DIM_A increases DIM_B in one range and decreases in another

4. Constraint influence
   DIM_A restricts the upper/lower bound of DIM_B

5. Inversion influence
   DIM_A rising causes DIM_B to fall in one cycle and rise in another

6. Shock influence
   DIM_A sudden jump causes DIM_B volatility

7. Drift influence
   DIM_A slow-change produces long-run DIM_B degradation

8. Stabilizing influence
   DIM_A buffers DIM_B against external shocks

Each cell in the 12×12 matrix uses one (and only one) of these.

---------------------------------------------------------
III. META-EQUATIONS (FULL LIST)
---------------------------------------------------------
Below are the 22 universal meta-equations governing global system behaviour.

These do not refer to any specific country — they define universal behaviour.

1. SYSTEM_CAPACITY:
   C_total = Σ (INFRA + TECH + ENERGY + DEMO_workforce_quality)

2. SYSTEM_DEMAND:
   D_total = Σ (DEMO_population + MARKET_demand_intensity)

3. STABILITY:
   S = 1 / (1 + (shock_index + volatility_index))

4. OVERLOAD:
   Ω = D_total / C_total

5. FRAGMENTATION:
   F = 1 - cohesion_index

6. COHESION:
   H = rule_following_index × social_trust × political_stability

7. DRIFT:
   DR = Σ (informal_power_strength × bureaucracy_depth × friction)

8. RECOVERY:
   R = (C_total × H) / Ω

9. ECONOMIC_GROWTH:
   g = productivity × investment × (1 - DR)

10. SOCIAL_TENSION:
    T = youth_unrest + unemployment + price_shock_sensitivity

11. MOBILITY_BEHAVIOUR:
    Mb = modal_split_vector × congestion_factor × income_distribution

12. ENERGY_STABILITY:
    Es = grid_stability / (peak_load × climate_risk)

13. DEMAND_SHOCK:
    d_t = ΔMARKET + ΔECON + ΔSOCIAL_events

14. SUPPLY_SHOCK:
    s_t = ΔINFRA_breakdown + ΔENERGY_failure

15. POLITICAL_VOLATILITY:
    Pv = election_cycle_variance + leadership_turnover

16. REGULATORY_DRIFT:
    Rd = bureaucracy_depth × informal_power_strength × rule_confusion

17. CRISIS_PROBABILITY:
    C_prob = f(Ω, F, Pv, Es, climate_risk)

18. RECOVERY_TIME:
    Rt = Ω / (H × investment_rate)

19. TECHNOLOGY_UPGRADE_SPEED:
    Tu = digital_adoption × education × investment

20. CULTURE_ALIGNMENT_INDEX:
    Cai = (power_distance × collectivism × rule-following)

21. PARTNERSHIP_FAILURE:
    Pf = corruption_friction + approval_delay_risk + informal_block

22. CONSUMPTION_INDEX:
    Ci = price_sensitivity × income × stability

---------------------------------------------------------
IV. SHOCK TRANSMISSION LAYER
---------------------------------------------------------
This defines how shocks propagate across dimensions.

SHOCK TYPES:
1. political_shock
2. economic_shock
3. social_shock
4. infrastructure_shock
5. environmental_shock
6. energy_shock
7. market_shock

SHOCK PATHWAYS:
Each shock can propagate in 4 channels:
A. Vertical (national → sector)
B. Horizontal (sector → sector)
C. Diagonal (sector → social → political)
D. Feedback loop (back into same dimension)

Example:
ENVIRONMENTAL_SHOCK → ENERGY → ECON → SOCIAL → POLC

---------------------------------------------------------
V. DRIFT VECTORS
---------------------------------------------------------
Drift is slow degradation. It has 6 vectors:

1. demographic_drift
2. economic_drift
3. governance_drift
4. social_drift
5. infrastructure_drift
6. behavioural_drift

Each drift vector reduces system stability over years or decades.

---------------------------------------------------------
VI. RECOVERY CHANNELS
---------------------------------------------------------
Recovery occurs through:

1. investment_recovery
2. governance_simplification
3. technological_upgrade
4. infrastructure_repair
5. social_stabilization
6. market_confidence_repair
7. emergency_policy_alignment

---------------------------------------------------------
VII. GLOBAL PREDICTIVE COHERENCE RULES
---------------------------------------------------------
For forecasts to be valid:
- drift must be monotonic unless shock intervention occurs
- stability must remain > 0.1
- energy_stability cannot fall below disaster threshold for >3 cycles
- governance oscillation must not exceed 2 cycles in 4 years
- demographic dependency cannot exceed 1.0 without economic compensation
- market_price_elasticity must align with income_distribution

=========================
END OF PART 2/60
=========================

==========================================
GLOBAL COUNTRY ENGINE — BASE SCHEMA v1.0
==========================================

This block defines:
- the universal data structure for every country,
- the canonical order of variables,
- the full attribute taxonomy (12 dimensions × 180+ variables),
- the deterministic formatting rules required to keep the engine coherent.

All 195 countries will later instantiate this schema without deviation.
This ensures every country is comparable, computable, and predictable.

---------------------------------------------------------
I. COUNTRY OBJECT — DEFINITIVE STRUCTURAL FORM
---------------------------------------------------------
Each country is represented using the following canonical object:

COUNTRY_OBJECT {
    country_code: ISO3,
    country_name: string,

    demographic_state: DEMOGRAPHIC_STATE_OBJECT,
    economic_structure: ECONOMIC_STRUCTURE_OBJECT,
    governance_structure: GOVERNANCE_STRUCTURE_OBJECT,
    political_cycle: POLITICAL_CYCLE_OBJECT,
    social_behaviour: SOCIAL_BEHAVIOUR_OBJECT,
    cultural_archetype: CULTURAL_ARCHETYPE_OBJECT,
    infrastructure_state: INFRASTRUCTURE_STATE_OBJECT,
    technology_state: TECHNOLOGY_STATE_OBJECT,
    mobility_state: MOBILITY_STATE_OBJECT,
    energy_state: ENERGY_STATE_OBJECT,
    environmental_state: ENVIRONMENTAL_STATE_OBJECT,
    market_behaviour: MARKET_BEHAVIOUR_OBJECT,

    risk_meta: COUNTRY_RISK_META,
    cycle_meta: COUNTRY_CYCLE_META,
    cluster_tag: CULTURAL_CLUSTER_TAG,
    economic_group_tag: ECONOMIC_GROUP_TAG,
    income_group_tag: INCOME_GROUP_TAG,
    regional_tag: REGIONAL_TAG
}

==========================================================
This layer establishes:
- 5 global regions

- regional multipliers
- structural patterns
- drift vectors
- alignment biases

- climate pressures
- mobility tendency
- EV adoption friction
- governance cycle pattern
- social tension structure

Every country inherits these as base weights BEFORE its own overrides.

==========================================================
GLOBAL COUNTRY GENERATION ENGINE — TEMPLATE v1.0
==========================================================
This template defines HOW every country is generated under
the Universe Engine architecture.

Each country inherits:
1. Regional Defaults (from Part 4)
2. Country Overrides
3. Country Multipliers
4. Structural Coherence Checks
5. Behavioural System Patterns
6. Economic Gravity Model
7. Political Cycle Model
8. Cultural Overlay Model
9. Infrastructure Feasibility Model
10. Mobility & Energy Pattern Model

This generates:
- National behaviour matrix
- Economic state
- Stability state
- Power state
- Market state
- Human systems overlays
- Technology readiness
- Climate load
- EV feasibility
- 30/90/180-day risk window

==========================================================
I. COUNTRY OBJECT SPECIFICATION
==========================================================
COUNTRY_OBJECT {
    iso_code,
    name,
    region,

    # Demographic
    population,
    youth_ratio,
    aging_ratio,
    birth_rate,
    migration_pattern,

    # Economic
    gdp,
    gdp_per_capita,
    inflation_rate,
    currency_volatility,
    informal_economy_ratio,
    sector_mix,
    income_distribution,

    # Governance
    bureaucracy_strength,
    corruption_load,
    formal_vs_informal_power,
    regulation_efficiency,
    permit_friction,

    # Politics
    political_system,
    election_cycle_length,
    polarization_level,
    stability_index,
    protest_risk,

    # Society
    collectivism_level,
    trust_in_institutions,
    gender_gap,
    education_quality,
    urban_rural_split,

    # Culture
    negotiation_style,
    power_distance,
    communication_style,
    time_orientation,
    hierarchy_model,

    # Infrastructure
    roads_quality,
    logistics_efficiency,
    grid_stability,
    internet_penetration,
    data_center_capacity,

    # Technology
    digital_adoption,
    mobile_first_index,
    tech_maturity,
    fintech_penetration,
    cybersecurity_level,

    # Mobility
    motorcycle_ratio,
    car_ratio,
    public_transport_quality,
    congestion_pattern,
    ride-hailing_penetration,

    # Energy
    renewables_ratio,
    fossil_dependency,
    price_volatility,
    power_loss_ratio,
    energy_security_index,

    # Environment
    climate_risks,
    disaster_frequency,
    pollution_level,
    heat_stress,
    flood_risk,

    # Market
    brand_loyalty,
    price_sensitivity,
    consumer_confidence,
    middle_class_size,
    e-commerce_penetration,

    # Derived System Indices
    national_stability,
    ev_feasibility,
    national_risk_score,

    # Time Cycles
    socio_political_cycle,
    economic_cycle,
    climate_cycle,
    cultural_cycle,
}

==========================================================
II. COUNTRY MULTIPLIER MODEL
==========================================================
Each country applies a 7-layer multiplier system:

1. REGIONAL_MULTIPLIER (from Part 4)
2. HISTORICAL_MULTIPLIER
   - colonial legacy
   - previous conflict
   - developmental path
   - institutional age

3. ECONOMIC_MULTIPLIER
   - trade openness
   - industrial base
   - foreign investment dependency
   - export structure

4. GOVERNANCE_MULTIPLIER
   - judicial independence
   - regulatory coherence
   - anticorruption strength
   - federal/local power split

5. SOCIOCULTURAL_MULTIPLIER
   - language family
   - religion cluster
   - identity cohesion
   - migration history

6. INFRASTRUCTURE_MULTIPLIER
   - geographic constraints
   - density model
   - climate engineering readiness
   - logistics corridors

7. TECHNOLOGY_MULTIPLIER
   - AI readiness
   - digital identity systems
   - open-data maturity
   - telecommunication investments

==========================================================
III. NATIONAL STABILITY MODEL
==========================================================
NATIONAL_STABILITY = f(
    governance_efficiency,
    corruption_load,
    inequality,
    protest_risk,
    political_polarization,
    climate_risk,
    infrastructure_resilience,
    energy_security
)

Scale: 0.0 → 1.0
- <0.30 = unstable
- 0.30–0.55 = fragile
- 0.55–0.75 = stable
- >0.75 = highly stable

==========================================================
IV. EV FEASIBILITY MODEL
==========================================================
EV_FEASIBILITY = f(
    grid_stability,
    income_level,
    fossil_subsidy_level,
    EV_infrastructure,
    tech_adoption,
    mobility_pattern,
    climate_load
)

Outputs:
- 0.0–0.25 = infeasible
- 0.25–0.50 = low feasibility
- 0.50–0.75 = medium feasibility
- 0.75–1.00 = high feasibility

==========================================================
V. NATIONAL RISK SCORE MODEL (30/90/180 DAY)
==========================================================
RISK_SCORE = f(
    political_risk,
    climate_risk,
    infrastructure_risk,
    currency_risk,
    market_shock,
    social_unrest_risk
)

Outputs:
- Short term (30 days)
- Medium term (90 days)
- Long term (180 days)

==========================================================
VI. POWER STRUCTURE MODEL
==========================================================
Every country fits into one of 8 power-structure archetypes:

1. Formal-State-Driven
2. Informal-Elite-Driven
3. Hybrid Dual-Power
4. Administrative-Heavy
5. Local-Centric
6. Clan/Sectarian
7. Corporate-Influenced
8. Geopolitical-Dependent

Each impacts:
- decision speed
- political friction
- project approvals
- EV adoption
- infrastructure timelines

==========================================================
VII. BEHAVIOURAL OVERLAY MODEL
==========================================================
Every country applies cultural overlays:

1. WORK BEHAVIOR
   - pace
   - ownership
   - conflict style
   - hierarchy use
   - rule interpretation

2. NEGOTIATION STYLE
   - direct / indirect
   - relationship-first / contract-first

3. TRUST MODEL
   - institutional trust
   - interpersonal trust
   - network-based trust

4. POLITICAL SENSITIVITY
   - speech boundaries
   - media response cycles
   - informal influence channels

==========================================================
VIII. COUNTRY CYCLE MODEL
==========================================================
1. SOCIO-POLITICAL CYCLE
   - election
   - leadership rotation
   - protest season
   - administrative changes

2. ECONOMIC CYCLE
   - peak
   - slowdown
   - recession
   - recovery

3. CLIMATE CYCLE
   - rainy
   - dry
   - storm
   - heat

4. CULTURAL CYCLE
   - holidays
   - migration seasons
   - festival cycles

==========================================================
IX. COUNTRY GENERATION OUTPUT FORMAT
==========================================================
Generated output always includes:

1. Country overview
2. 9-dimension structural index
3. National stability score
4. EV feasibility score
5. Risk forecast (30/90/180 days)
6. Power map
7. Behavioural profile
8. Sectoral dynamics
9. Policy friction zones
10. Infrastructure bottlenecks
11. Energy transition pathway
12. Market-cycle projection

==========================================================
END OF PART 5/60
==========================================================
